<div id="review_35535015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35535015" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35535015?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2013">read2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=around-the-usa">around-the-usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=location-usa-illinois">location-usa-illinois</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35535015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5169650608142214938">This is the first book I finished from my <a href='http://readingenvy.blogspot.com/2013/04/book-speed-dating-report.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>speed dating project</a>, so that probably tells you something about the ease of reading this story about Frank Lloyd Wright's mistress and the rise and fall of their relationship. I had originally picked this book to use as my Illinois pick for the Around the USA reading challenge, and still will count it for that since Wright's main office was in Chicago during the timeframe of this book, but it also takes place in Italy and Wisconsin.<br/><br/>I have seen several p</span>
  <span id="freeText5169650608142214938" style="display:none">This is the first book I finished from my <a href="http://readingenvy.blogspot.com/2013/04/book-speed-dating-report.html" rel="nofollow noopener">speed dating project</a>, so that probably tells you something about the ease of reading this story about Frank Lloyd Wright's mistress and the rise and fall of their relationship. I had originally picked this book to use as my Illinois pick for the Around the USA reading challenge, and still will count it for that since Wright's main office was in Chicago during the timeframe of this book, but it also takes place in Italy and Wisconsin.<br /><br />I have seen several people, mostly mothers, rating this book low because they don't like that FLW's mistress, Mamah Cheney, left her children to be with Frank. I think it is kudos to the author that she is able to bring these characters to life - to make a reader hate a character, even a historical one, is a feat. There is one character in this novel that I hated far more, and that would be Frank Lloyd Wright himself. So completely self-centered. So delusional as to believe his artistic vision was more important than paying his staff or respecting others. So selfish that his emotional needs came first, with no regard for the needs of the woman who has left her family for him, and severed all her ties. <br /><br />Why do women give up their lives to be with selfish men? This is something I will never understand. It isn't an accident that the novel is called "Loving Frank," and not "Frank Loving Other People." Mamah tries to regain her sense of purpose by translating the works of a Swedish feminist, and she tries too late to rebuild relationships with her children and sister, but Frank is not supportive of anything taking energy away from his needs. Ugh. What a baby. And in the end, she pays dearly for it. I could not believe the end of this book. It felt like one of those terrible movie endings intended to shock the audience, but I went back and read about it and it is all true. I really didn't know much about Wright after all. <br /><br />And as far as Mamah goes, well clearly her life went the wrong direction the minute she gave up her life as a librarian to marry Edwin. :)<br /><br />ETA a few quotables:<br /><br />"All the talk revolves around getting the vote. That should go without saying. There's so much more personal freedom to gain beyond that. Yet women are part of the problem. We plan dinner parties and make flowers out of crepe paper. Too many of us make small lives for ourselves."<br /><br />"People who live only for their children make bad company for them."</span>
  <a data-text-id="5169650608142214938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_32181516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32181516" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1499886-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238186677p2/1499886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32181516?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/1499886-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32181516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9276093900494553599">Living in Chicago, I have visited Wright's Home & Studio in Oak Park and Taliesin in Spring Green many times, so I already knew the stories of the great architect's personal tragedies and failings. Loving Frank was an engaging read, but I found myself questioning some of it, particularly Horan's depiction of Mamah's guilt and regret over her abandonment of her children. I wanted to like Mamah, but I found that -- even though Horan tried hard to convince me to empathize with her -- I couldn't ful</span>
  <span id="freeText9276093900494553599" style="display:none">Living in Chicago, I have visited Wright's Home &amp; Studio in Oak Park and Taliesin in Spring Green many times, so I already knew the stories of the great architect's personal tragedies and failings. Loving Frank was an engaging read, but I found myself questioning some of it, particularly Horan's depiction of Mamah's guilt and regret over her abandonment of her children. I wanted to like Mamah, but I found that -- even though Horan tried hard to convince me to empathize with her -- I couldn't fully understand or excuse her selfishness. Wright's arrogance and disregard for the feelings of others are legendary, and knowing what I do about his later years and subsequent marriage, I couldn't quite persuade myself that Mamah really was the love of his life. In the end, I finished the book with my ideas about Wright mostly unchanged. Wright was a professionally arrogant but personally insecure man who needed adoring disciples -- male and female -- around him at all times to reflect his greatness. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9276093900494553599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5128865280745187697">A wonderful education on Frank Lloyd Wright's motivation and personality told through the viewpoint of Mamah Borthwick-Cheney, his mistress. <br/><br/>As I read this book, I tried to pinpoint why I never had a problem picking this book up as it saddened me and at times maddened me. By the time I came to the end I knew why - the author does a terrific job of presenting this fictional history (based on fact) unbiased. I love authors who trust their readers enough to let them make their own judgments and don</span>
  <span id="freeText5128865280745187697" style="display:none">A wonderful education on Frank Lloyd Wright's motivation and personality told through the viewpoint of Mamah Borthwick-Cheney, his mistress. <br /><br />As I read this book, I tried to pinpoint why I never had a problem picking this book up as it saddened me and at times maddened me. By the time I came to the end I knew why - the author does a terrific job of presenting this fictional history (based on fact) unbiased. I love authors who trust their readers enough to let them make their own judgments and don't feel they need to "help" them. Nice job of writing.<br /><br />Just curious, (this is totally off-topic), but does anyone else see the lower part of a woman's face reflected in the stained glass in the bottom left of the book cover? <div id="review_36129364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36129364" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/307208-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233177432p2/307208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36129364?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/307208-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36129364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10374314124568251311">This book was brought to my attention several months ago but I didn't seriously consider reading it because I thought it was essentially a biography of Frank Lloyd Wright, the famous architect. I have a serious handicap when it comes to reading non-fiction and if I'm going to read a biography of someone, I wanted to read about someone whose life's details I had some...nay....any interest in knowing. An architect, even a really, really famous one, didn't meet that criteria.<br/><br/>When it was selected as</span>
  <span id="freeText10374314124568251311" style="display:none">This book was brought to my attention several months ago but I didn't seriously consider reading it because I thought it was essentially a biography of Frank Lloyd Wright, the famous architect. I have a serious handicap when it comes to reading non-fiction and if I'm going to read a biography of someone, I wanted to read about someone whose life's details I had some...nay....any interest in knowing. An architect, even a really, really famous one, didn't meet that criteria.<br /><br />When it was selected as a book group selection, I waved my white flag and read it anyway. Say what you will about book groups, one thing I appreciate about the forum is that they tend to throw books in my path that I wouldn't otherwise read. When I end up actually enjoying the mandated book, I appreciate the selection even more.<br /><br />Loving Frank is part factual biography, part fictional novel featuring the life of Mamah Borthwick Cheney's as she fell in love with Frank Lloyd Wright. Mamah, a feminist, intellectual and suffragist, was married to safe, loyal but rather boring Edwin Cheney. The married couple were financially secure enough to keep a nanny, a housekeeper and eventually hire an up and coming architect to build one of his conceptually new "Prairie Houses". Financial and marital security did not bring contentment to Mamah, however, and when Wright intimately connects with her on an intellectual and emotional level during the building of her and her husband's home, a physical affair between the two quickly follows.<br /><br />What makes this story compelling and great discussion fodder isn't Frank and Mamah's relationship or their affair, it's the constant negotiating and justification the author forces Mamah to debate with herself and with the world about the honesty and integrity of romantic and self love. For Mamah, a person's own happiness super ceded that of any one else's, including one's children, although she admitted several times how incongruous that belief felt at times. When she found literature written by radical thinker, Ellen Key, her belief that she should be with Frank at the expense of everything else, because she loved him, deepened. I am left wondering when, if ever, a selfish act is the BEST act. As much as the pair wished it to be so, they did not exist in a bubble and their relationship had real and lasting consequences to the families they abandoned.<br /><br />If the moral debate is the actual gift of the book (and for me, it was), then the fancy wrapping and giant bow is the holy-cow-wow! drama and historically significant events that made up the life of Frank Lloyd Wright. This should be a very interesting discussion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10374314124568251311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_157777466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157777466" />
    <a title="Susan (aka Just My Op)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489613-susan-aka-just-my-op"><img alt="Susan (aka Just My Op)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549168469p2/2489613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157777466?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan (aka Just My Op)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan (aka Just My Op)" href="/user/show/2489613-susan-aka-just-my-op">Susan (aka Just My Op)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489613-susan-aka-just-my-op?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489613-susan-aka-just-my-op?shelf=group-reads">group-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157777466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16658517722892172059">The ending did surprise me – I didn't see that coming. If you don't know it, I'm not telling.<br/><br/>Although I'm somewhat familiar with his architecture, I knew little (and still know relatively little) of Frank Lloyd Wright's personal life. And I knew nothing of Mamah Borthwick Cheney. I like historical fiction that has been well researched, as this book apparently was. Still, it just didn't work for me.<br/><br/>Mamah left her husband and children to be with Frank. She abandoned her children with a friend in B</span>
  <span id="freeText16658517722892172059" style="display:none">The ending did surprise me – I didn't see that coming. If you don't know it, I'm not telling.<br /><br />Although I'm somewhat familiar with his architecture, I knew little (and still know relatively little) of Frank Lloyd Wright's personal life. And I knew nothing of Mamah Borthwick Cheney. I like historical fiction that has been well researched, as this book apparently was. Still, it just didn't work for me.<br /><br />Mamah left her husband and children to be with Frank. She abandoned her children with a friend in Boulder, not even waiting until her husband could come get them. This was supposedly all because of her great love for Frank, who designed her and her husband's house. I just didn't feel the love. It was there on paper – she loved him enough to abandon her life, but the feelings just didn't come through. To me, it felt more like she was using this great love as an excuse to escape her responsibilities.<br /><br />I was annoyed that she seemed to use the suffrage movement as an excuse for her action. She didn't seem to really fight for it, really care about it other than as a justification, a movement that she used to provide her an excuse for bad decisions. I just never grew to like her.<br /><br />Frank Lloyd Wright came across as a childish, self-centered, spoiled cheat, excusing all his shortcomings because he had talent. Mamah should have kicked him to the curb.<br /><br />The story, even if I didn't much care for the two central characters, could have entertained me. But the writing just didn't pull me in. I couldn't feel the emotion that was supposed to be so prominent. There were a couple of discrepancies that took my mind from the story, such as her Swedish professor being male on one page, female two pages later. Were there two professors? Did one leave and another start? Explain, please. I'm easily enough confused. Put this all together and Mamah may have loved Frank but I didn't love Frank or Mamah or this book.<br /><br />This book was a selection for my fact-to-face book club that meets in a couple of days. It will be interesting to see what others thought.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16658517722892172059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_4292334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4292334" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101159-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579229854p2/101159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4292334?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/101159-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/101159-andrea?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer4292334&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4292334" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17466154430252687386">I got my hands on an advanced reader's edition the day before it was released. I still feel special.<br/><br/>This historical novel chronicles the emotional love affair between famous architect Frank Lloyd Wright and little-known translator/feminist scholar Mamah Borthwick. The story, which follows Mamah's (pronounced "May-muh") perspective, took the author more than seven years to carefully research. Horan's writing is crisp and beautiful--I felt as though everything I read was what <i>really</i> happened, even</span>
  <span id="freeText17466154430252687386" style="display:none">I got my hands on an advanced reader's edition the day before it was released. I still feel special.<br /><br />This historical novel chronicles the emotional love affair between famous architect Frank Lloyd Wright and little-known translator/feminist scholar Mamah Borthwick. The story, which follows Mamah's (pronounced "May-muh") perspective, took the author more than seven years to carefully research. Horan's writing is crisp and beautiful--I felt as though everything I read was what <i>really</i> happened, even though I knew that the author took some liberties with the facts. She certainly did justice to the memory of her "characters."<br /><br />For days I've been consumed by this delicate and heart wrenching tale. There I was, almost finished and already planning to give it four stars. And then, I read the ending. Jeeee-sus! I realize that this story is based in history, and that the author didn't just pull the idea out of nowhere, but, <i>crap</i>. The whole now-I'm-having-nightmares factor knocked my rating down to three stars. I suppose you could argue that an author's power to shake me up so badly is a plus--Horan is indeed a fantastic writer. And besides the ending, I loved this story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17466154430252687386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3064377566" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3064377566" />
    <a title="Therese" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15300646-therese"><img alt="Therese" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581736210p2/15300646.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3064377566?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Therese" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Therese" href="/user/show/15300646-therese">Therese</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781469234243" href="/book/show/15949203-loving-frank">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3064377566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10085133950190506652">You might say this is the story of Mamah Borthwick, a young woman who, in the early nineteen teens, wanted to make a difference and do great things. So she turned her life upside down to live an authentic and honest life. Or as her sister remarked, went off to discover her personality. Or you might say Mamah, a happily married woman turned her life upside down, abandoning her steady and loving husband, her comfortable life, and her children to attach herself to a married man with whom she’d fall</span>
  <span id="freeText10085133950190506652" style="display:none">You might say this is the story of Mamah Borthwick, a young woman who, in the early nineteen teens, wanted to make a difference and do great things. So she turned her life upside down to live an authentic and honest life. Or as her sister remarked, went off to discover her personality. Or you might say Mamah, a happily married woman turned her life upside down, abandoning her steady and loving husband, her comfortable life, and her children to attach herself to a married man with whom she’d fallen in love, her soulmate. Interestingly, that man was renowned architect Frank Lloyd Wright. I’m sure Mamah’s decisions about the best way to live her life are debatable, some feeling she should have stayed true to her family and others who might believe she was right to follow her heart. Despite how we may be inclined to judge, Mamah cut an interesting female figure of that time, and led her life as she saw fit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10085133950190506652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_9737617" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9737617" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/649979-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312019977p2/649979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9737617?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/649979-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Frank Lloyd Wright, architecture and the Women's Movement</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9737617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17420967245833975103">Awesome book--especially as a debut novel! The last 50 pages took me by surprise and kept me glued until the very end! I didn't know anything about Mamah Borthwick and knew very little about Frank Lloyd Wright, so it was surprising to read what happens in the end. If anything, Horan's narrative technique in the last 50 pages made the book for me.<br/><br/>Don't be fooled by the title, though. This book is so much more than a story about an illicit love affair and the scandal it caused--and so much more th</span>
  <span id="freeText17420967245833975103" style="display:none">Awesome book--especially as a debut novel! The last 50 pages took me by surprise and kept me glued until the very end! I didn't know anything about Mamah Borthwick and knew very little about Frank Lloyd Wright, so it was surprising to read what happens in the end. If anything, Horan's narrative technique in the last 50 pages made the book for me.<br /><br />Don't be fooled by the title, though. This book is so much more than a story about an illicit love affair and the scandal it caused--and so much more than the story of Frank Lloyd Wright's years with Mamah. If anything, this book is solely about Mamah Borthwick and her search "to find herself," and Nancy Horan gives voice to a woman that few know about and puts her in context in an era when women couldn't vote, work and be self-sufficient.<br /><br />There were times when I thought it plodding--Mamah's indecisions, regrets and, at times, selfishness--but I believe that was just Horan's way of impressing upon the reader the torturous emotions that Mamah must have felt about making one of the biggest decisions of her life--the ramifications of which can never be undone. It actually resulted in a more complex, conflicted character, one who isn't perfect, a woman that many in today's world could identify with. Makes me want to learn more about Frank Lloyd Wright and whether or not Mamah's influence can still be seen in his later artwork/architecture.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17420967245833975103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E281jvrgKsjh2+QiaEv3l0704K5Fph9+6hdu1TmeWo1t7wIrh0OpuumhuCWP9Y7Ff1GBz6+Zf3NAD/jQYA3czQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

researched Death in a Prairie House: Frank Lloyd Wright and the Taliesin Murders.     In response to the scandal generated by his open affair with the proto-feminist and free love advocate Mamah smoking hull.     Supplying both a gripping mystery story and an authoritative portrait of the artist as a young man, Drennan wades through the myths surrounding Wright and the massacre, casting fresh light on the formulation of Wright’s architectural ideology and the cataclysmic effects that the Taliesin murders exerted on the fabled architect and on his subsequent designs. Best Books for General An idealistic abolitionist, March has gone as chaplain to serve the Union cause. But the war tests his faith not only in the Union—which is also capable of barbarism and racism—but in himself. As he recovers from a near-fatal illness, March must reassemble and reconnect with his family, who have no idea of what he has endured.
